Vitamin K2 MK-7 150mcg With breakfast alongside D3 Always pair K2 with D3 — directs calcium to bones, not arteries.
Creatine monohydrate 5g Post-workout with breakfast Mix into oats or milk. On rest days: take with breakfast instead. No loading phase needed after initial.
Omega-3 fish oil 2g EPA+DHA With dinner (~7:00pm) Take with food to reduce fishy burps. Check label — dose to achieve 2g combined EPA+DHA, not just total oil.
Zinc picolinate 30mg With dinner (~7:00pm) Picolinate form has good absorption. Do not take on empty stomach.
Magnesium glycinate 400mg 9:15pm with small snack Glycinate form: gentle, non-laxative, supports sleep quality and muscle recovery. Small snack = handful of nuts.
Whey protein 30g Post-workout mixed with 250ml cold milk Only use if daily protein from food falls short of 130g. Not mandatory if meals are on target.

Key rules:
- D3 + K2 always together, always with fat
- Collagen + Vitamin C always paired, always 15 min pre-workout (not on rest days)
- Magnesium at night — do not take in the morning, reduces sleep benefit
- Creatine timing is flexible; consistency matters more than exact window

3. Daily Meal Templates

Training Day (~2,100 kcal | 130g protein)

Time Meal Foods Protein Kcal
7:15am Pre-workout primer Collagen 15g + Vit C source (½ glass OJ or 1 kiwi) + 1 medium banana ~15g ~190
8:30am Breakfast (post-workout) ½ cup dry steel-cut oats (cooked overnight) + 3 soft-boiled eggs + 1 tbsp peanut butter + 1 cup (250ml) fresh milk + D3/K2 + Creatine 5g ~42g ~550
1:00pm Lunch (office salad bowl) Build your bowl: ~130g chicken breast or thigh + 1 hard-boiled egg + ½ scoop potato salad + tomato + celery + salsa. Chicken breast = leaner; thigh = slightly more fat, more flavour. Both hit the protein target. ~42–45g ~450
4:00pm Afternoon snack 1 handful mixed nuts (almonds, cashews, walnuts ~30g) + 1 apple ~7g ~220
7:00pm Dinner (home-cooked) 180g grilled/baked chicken breast OR 150g salmon OR 200g lean pork loin + ½ cup cooked brown rice + stir-fried vegetables (kangkong, broccoli, tofu optional — any combo) + Omega-3 + Zinc ~42g ~580
9:15pm Evening wind-down 150g Greek yoghurt (full-fat or 2%) + Magnesium glycinate 400mg ~18g ~180
Total ~163g* ~2,170*

Protein and calories are estimates. If dinner protein is lower (e.g. 120g salmon), skip or reduce the nut snack. Whey protein shake (30g + 250ml milk = ~42g protein, ~250 kcal) only if you are short on protein from food — do not default to using it every day.

Rest Day (~1,950 kcal | 120–130g protein)

Time Meal Foods Protein Kcal
8:00am Breakfast Same oats + 3 eggs + peanut butter + milk + D3/K2 + Creatine 5g (here, not post-workout) ~42g ~550
1:00pm Lunch Same office salad bowl as training day ~42–45g ~450
4:00pm Afternoon snack 15g nuts + 1 small fruit ~4g ~150
7:00pm Dinner Same as training day template ~42g ~580
9:15pm Evening wind-down 100g Greek yoghurt + Magnesium glycinate 400mg ~10g ~130
Total ~140g ~1,970

Rest day adjustments: Skip the pre-workout collagen + banana (saves ~190 kcal). Reduce afternoon snack and evening yoghurt portions slightly. Dinner stays the same — protein target still applies even on rest days for muscle protein synthesis.

4. Weekly Training Schedule Overview

Day Session Focus Time
Monday Strength Day A Hinge + Push (superset format) 7:30–8:00am
Tuesday Strength Day B Squat + TGU (superset format) 7:30–8:00am
Wednesday Rest Active recovery — 20–30 min walk, foam roll —
Thursday Strength Day C Vertical Pull + Push + Single-Leg + Power 7:30–8:00am
Friday Strength Day D Full Body + Jump Power 7:30–8:00am
Saturday Rucking (Zone 2) 8–10kg pack, 35–45 min, neighbourhood/park connector 7:00–8:00am
Sunday Family Swimming Zone 1–2 active recovery 4:00pm

Zone 2 target for age 42: Heart rate 107–125 bpm (180 − 42 = 138 max; Zone 2 = ~65–90% aerobic threshold). For rucking, aim for the lower end — pack weight will push HR up. You should be able to hold a conversation but feel consistently warm.

Why staying in Zone 2 matters — not Zone 3 or higher: Once HR climbs above ~125 bpm into Zone 3 (the "grey zone"), you shift from predominantly fat oxidation to carbohydrate burning, and the training stimulus changes entirely. Zone 3 is neither easy enough to recover from nor hard enough to build true cardiovascular capacity — it produces fatigue without the mitochondrial adaptations you want. For someone doing 4 hard strength sessions per week, a Zone 3+ ruck is an unplanned fifth hard session that accumulates systemic fatigue and impairs recovery for Monday's training. Zone 2 keeps the aerobic system developing (PGC-1α signalling, mitochondrial biogenesis, improved fat oxidation) while leaving the body fresh for strength work. If your HR spikes — uphill section, heavier pack, Singapore heat — slow your pace or pause briefly to let it drop back down.

5. The 4 Training Days — Detailed

Each session is 30 minutes: 2 min warm-up, ~22 min main work (block pairs), 3–5 min prehab/core finisher. Blocks pair antagonist or non-competing movements — you rest one muscle group while working another, making 30 minutes as productive as a conventional 45-minute session. Rest: 45 sec between sets (W1/W3/W4), 90 sec (W2 strength week). KB swings on Monday and Thursday only; Friday uses broad/box jumps as the power stimulus.

Day A — Hinge + Push (Monday, 7:30–8:00am)

Purpose: Build horizontal push and pull strength as the primary strength pair (Floor Press + Row); develop posterior chain via RDL; KB swings moved to a metcon finisher so the primary strength blocks run on a fully fresh posterior chain. Face pull doubles as active rest between heavy hinge sets, keeping HR in range without losing prehab benefit.

Movement patterns: Horizontal Push, Horizontal Pull, Hinge, Power Finisher

Warm-up (2 min):
- Band pull-apart: 2×15 (shoulder prehab activation — do before any pressing)
- Shoulder CARs (Controlled Articular Rotations): 5 slow circles each arm

Block A — Push/Pull Strength Pair (4 rounds, 45s rest — 90s rest in W2):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
A1: DB Floor Press Lie on floor, DB in hands, elbows at 45° from torso. Floor stops descent — shoulder safety mechanism. Full lockout at top. Controlled eccentric.
A2: Single-arm DB Row Immediately after the press. Knee and hand on floor. Pull elbow past hip. No shoulder elevation. Feel lat contraction at top.

HR rule: start each set below 130 bpm — check before picking up the DBs.

Block B — Hinge + Active Rest (4 rounds, same rest as Block A):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
B1: DB Romanian Deadlift Soft knee bend, push hips back, DBs stay close to legs, feel stretch in hamstrings at bottom. Neutral spine throughout.
B2: Band Face Pull (active rest) 2×15 — pull to forehead level, elbows high, thumbs back at end position. Slotted here deliberately: HR drops faster than passive rest and the prehab is done before the finisher.

Finisher — KB Swing Metcon:
- W1: 4 rounds × 8 reps | moderate KB | 30s rest — re-establish hip hinge mechanics; write down the KB weight
- W2: 6 rounds × 6 reps | heavy KB | 30s rest — maximal power every single rep
- W3: 3 rounds × 12 reps | moderate KB | 30s rest — consistent power; every rep should look like the first
- W4: 2 rounds × 8 reps | light KB | 30s rest — perfect mechanics only; no fatigue grinding

Core:
- Dead Bug: 2×8/side — lower back pressed firmly into floor throughout; lower opposite arm/leg slowly

Day B — Squat + TGU (Tuesday, 7:30–8:00am)

Purpose: Build squat strength through full range; Turkish Get-Up (TGU) addresses shoulder stability and full-body integration — critical for long-term shoulder health. TGU is performed solo (cannot be superseted — it demands full focus). Goblet squat and farmer carry are paired as a metabolic superset.

Movement patterns: Shoulder Stability, Squat, Carry/Core

Warm-up (2 min):
- Glute bridge: 2×10 (activate glutes before squat)
- BW goblet squat: 2×8 (elbows inside knees at bottom, chest tall)

Turkish Get-Up — 3 sets × 2 reps/side (W4: 2 sets × 2 reps/side):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
Turkish Get-Up (TGU) Do this first while completely fresh — it demands full concentration. Move slowly through each phase. Never rush a TGU. KB arm stays locked vertical throughout. Scan the KB at all times.

Rest between sides: 90 seconds (W1/W3/W4) | 2 minutes (W2) — TGU is a skill movement; treat rest like a skill drill, not a muscle set.

Block A — Squat + Carry (4 rounds, 45s rest — 90s rest in W2):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
A1: KB Goblet Squat KB at chest, elbows up, chest tall. Sit into hips, knees track over toes. Full depth.
A2: KB Farmer Carry (20m) KB in one or both hands. Shoulders packed down and back. Tall posture, slight core brace. Do NOT lean to the loaded side.

Prehab Finisher (4 min):
- Band face pull: 2×15 — pull to forehead level, elbows high, thumbs back at end position
- RKC Plank: 2×20 sec — tuck pelvis, squeeze glutes, pull elbows toward toes, pull toes toward elbows. Total body tension.

Day C — Vertical Pull + Push + Single-Leg + Power (Thursday, 7:30–8:00am)

Purpose: Pull-up + push-up as the primary strength pair — introduces the vertical pull pattern missing from Days A and B, creating balanced pulling stimulus across the week. Power and single-leg work follow as Block B. Suitcase carry stands alone so it can be loaded and executed with full focus.

Movement patterns: Vertical Pull, Horizontal Push (RPE 6 max), Power/Hinge, Single-Leg Squat, Carry

Warm-up (2 min):
- Band Y-T-W: 2×8 each position — do this before any pressing; activates lower traps and rotator cuff
- Y: arms at ~135° (overhead Y shape), thumbs up
- T: arms at 90° (T shape), thumbs up
- W: elbows bent, pull band, squeeze shoulder blades
- Shoulder CARs: 5 each arm

Block A — Vertical Pull + Push (3 rounds, 45s rest — 90s rest in W2):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
A1: Pull-up (3-sec eccentric) Full hang at bottom. Pull until chin clears bar. 3-second controlled lower on every rep — this is the strength stimulus. Auto-regulate reps by round: W1 = 4 / 3 / 3
A2: Push-up variation (RPE 6 max) Immediately after the pull-up set — no rest between A1 and A2. Pull-up and push-up are antagonists, so the push-up starts on a relatively fresh chest. W1/W3/W4: 8 reps

Rest 90s after completing both A1 + A2, then repeat.

Block B — Power + Single-Leg (4 rounds W1/W2 | 3 rounds W3 | 2 rounds W4 — 45s rest W1/W3/W4 | 90s rest W2):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
B1: KB Swing Hike it back (not squat down), explosive hip extension, glutes squeeze at top. This is a hip hinge, not a squat. W2: heavier KB than W1.
B2: DB Reverse Lunge Step back (not forward). Knee hovers 1–2cm above floor. Front foot stays flat. Control the descent.

Standalone:
- KB Suitcase Carry: 2×20m/side — KB in ONE hand only. Walk without leaning to the KB side — this is the entire challenge. Switch hands between sets. W2: heavier KB than W1.

Prehab Finisher (3 min):
- Bird dog: 2×6/side — opposite arm + leg extended, hold 2 sec at top, return without twisting hips

Day D — Full Body + Jump Power (Friday, 7:30–8:00am)

Purpose: Full-body integration to end the training week. Broad/Box jump replaces Friday swings — this keeps swings to Mon + Thu only (reducing cumulative posterior chain fatigue), adds a pure neural power stimulus with zero wrist load, and trains explosive hip extension with a fresh movement pattern. BSS paired with clean + press as an antagonist superset. Bent-over row stands alone so it can be loaded to maximum.

Movement patterns: Jump Power, Single-Leg Squat, Push (RPE 6 max), Pull

Warm-up (2 min):
- Band pull-apart: 2×15
- Hip circles: 10 each direction

Power Opener (4 rounds W1/W2 | 3 rounds W3 | 2 rounds W4 — 45s rest W1/W3/W4 | 90s rest W2):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
Broad Jump or Box Jump Full reset between every rep — step back, reset posture, then jump. This is not a continuous movement. Land soft: absorb with hips and knees, not a stiff landing. W1: submaximal — 4×4, focus on landing mechanics and hip drive. W2: maximal intent — 4×4. W3: 3×5, moderate effort. W4: 2×4, easy — focus on mechanics.

Block A — Single-Leg + Press (4 rounds W1/W2 | 3 rounds W3 | 2 rounds W4 — same rest as Power Opener):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
A1: Bulgarian Split Squat Rear foot elevated on sofa/sturdy chair ~45cm. DB in each hand. Lower until rear knee hovers above floor. Front shin stays near vertical. This will be humbling — that is correct.
A2: KB Single-arm Clean + Press (press at RPE 6 max) Clean to rack, brief pause, then press. Press at RPE 6 max — strict shoulder-awareness. If any impingement sensation, stop the press and finish set as clean-only.

Block B — Pull Standalone (3 rounds W1/W2/W3 | 2 rounds W4 — same rest):

Exercise Cue / Key Technique Note
DB Bent-over Row Hinge to ~45°, DB in both hands. Row to hip crease, squeeze shoulder blades at top. Stands alone this session so you can load it properly — this is the heaviest pull of the week.

Core Finisher (3 min):
- Dead bug: 2×10/side — lower back pressed firmly into floor throughout
- Side plank: 2×20s/side — straight body alignment, top hip not drooping

6. 4-Week Undulating Periodisation

The principle: Intensity and volume rotate week-to-week across four distinct phases. This stops the body from accommodating to a fixed stimulus — a common plateau for advanced trainees. Movements stay constant; the stress variable changes.

Week Phase Superset Rounds Reps RPE Target Rest Between Supersets Notes
Week 1 Accumulation 4 rounds 8 7 45 sec Re-establish all movement patterns. Choose moderate weights. Track every weight used — this is your baseline.
Week 2 Strength 4 rounds 6 8 90 sec (120s if HR >130) Increase load from Week 1. Fewer reps, more weight, 90s rest minimum. Check HR before each set — start below 130 bpm. Swings on Mon + Thu only; Friday power is broad/box jump.
Week 3 Volume 3 rounds 12 7–8 45 sec Lighter than Week 2, but more total reps per set. Metabolic stress accumulates through superset density.
Week 4 Deload 2 rounds 8 5–6 45 sec 50% of Week 3's total volume. Same exercises, same form. Intentionally easy. This is where adaptation happens.

Cycle restart: After Week 4, return to Week 1 structure — but with heavier weights than the previous cycle's Week 1. This is progressive overload in action.

TGU exception: TGU does not follow the superset format and is performed solo. Sets and reps do not follow the main periodisation table:
- W1/W3: 3 sets × 2 reps/side
- W2: 3 sets × 2 reps/side — heavier KB, full concentration
- W4: 2 sets × 2 reps/side — light KB, quality only

7. Full 28-Day Calendar

How to read the calendar: Each training day shows the exercise, sets × reps for that week's phase, and any key notes. Rest days, rucking, and swimming days are also shown. Meals reference the templates in Section 3 unless noted otherwise.

Week 1 — Accumulation Phase (4 rounds × 8 reps | RPE 7)

Goal for the week: Re-establish movement patterns. Choose weights that feel moderately challenging — you should be able to complete all reps with good form and feel like you had 2–3 reps in reserve. Write down every weight used.

Activity: Rucking — 8–10kg pack. 35–45 min. Zone 2 pace. After a high-rep volume week, this will serve as excellent active recovery. Keep HR on the lower end of Zone 2 (107–115 bpm).

Day 21 — Sunday | Family Swimming

Supplements: Rest Day schedule

Meals: Rest Day template

Activity: Family swimming at 4:00pm. Easy effort. You are entering the last full training week before the deload — let this be restorative.

Week 4 — Deload Phase (2 rounds × 8 reps | RPE 5–6)

Goal for the week: Intentional reduction in volume and intensity. This is where supercompensation occurs — the body adapts to the previous 3 weeks of stress. Do not skip the deload or turn it into a "light week that still feels hard." RPE 5–6 means you could easily do 5 more reps. That is the goal.

Deload mindset: This is not a waste. Elite athletes take deloads. This week allows joints, tendons, and the nervous system to recover. You will feel stronger in Week 1 of the next cycle.

8. Progressive Overload Rules

When to Increase Load

Increase weight on an exercise when both of the following are true:
1. You completed all sets at the top of the rep range (e.g. all 8 reps in W1, all 5 in W2) with good form
2. RPE was ≤7 on the final set for 2 consecutive sessions of that exercise

Increments:
- Dumbbells: +2kg per DB (i.e. +4kg total load for bilateral exercises)
- Kettlebells: next size up (typically +4kg jumps — if the jump feels too large, split the difference using a resistance band as counterbalance or add a DB)
- Push-ups: advance one variation level (standard → close-grip → archer → pike)

When NOT to Increase Load

  • Form deteriorates at any rep before the prescribed rep count
  • RPE is 8+ across all sets (not just the last one)
  • During deload week — no increases regardless of how easy it feels
  • Any session where shoulder feels pre-symptomatic (even slightly "off")

The Shoulder Rule

This is non-negotiable and applies to every pressing and overhead movement:

  1. If you feel shoulder discomfort (not muscle burn — discomfort) at any point during a press: stop that set immediately
  2. Drop to the previous weight or a lower push-up variation for the remainder of the session
  3. Add 1 extra set of band face pulls (3×15 → 4×15) at the prehab finisher for that session
  4. Do not push through impingement — training through shoulder pain converts a minor issue into a structural problem. One skipped set costs nothing. One impingement flare-up costs 2–4 weeks.

Load Progression Across Cycles (Expected)

Exercise Cycle 1 W1 Target Cycle 2 W1 Target Cycle 3 W1 Target
KB Swing 20–24kg 24–28kg 28–32kg
DB RDL 2×16–20kg 2×20–24kg 2×22–26kg
DB Floor Press 2×14–18kg 2×16–20kg 2×18–22kg
KB Goblet Squat 20–24kg 24kg 28kg
Bulgarian Split Squat BW or 2×8kg 2×10–12kg 2×12–14kg

These are estimates based on your profile. Your actual starting weights may differ — use the W1 RPE 7 target as your calibration.

9. What to Track

Training Log (Every Session)

Keep a simple log — notebook, phone note, or app. Record after each session:

Field What to Write
Date e.g. Mon 24 Mar
Session e.g. Day A
Exercise Name
Weight used e.g. 2×18kg DB RDL
Sets × reps achieved e.g. 4×8 (all complete) or 4×8,8,8,7 (failed last rep)
RPE 1–10 scale
Notes e.g. "shoulder felt slightly tight on press rep 6 — stopped early; added face pull set"

Why this matters: Without logs, "I think I used 18kg last time" becomes your planning basis. With logs, you know exactly what to beat.

Weekly Check-In (Same Day Each Week — Recommended: Sunday Morning)

  • [ ] Bodyweight: Morning, post-void, before eating. Record in kg to 1 decimal. Same scale, same conditions.
  • [ ] Waist measurement: Around navel level. Relaxed (not sucked in). 1 measurement per week.
  • [ ] Sleep quality: Subjective 1–5 (helps correlate recovery with training output)
  • [ ] Energy levels: Subjective 1–5

Bodyweight target over 4 weeks: +0.5 to +1.0kg. This is a lean surplus — you are not trying to gain fast; slow gain preserves the lean frame and avoids excess fat. If weight is unchanged after 2 weeks, add 100–150 kcal/day (extra tablespoon peanut butter, handful of nuts, or extra half-cup rice).

Monthly Benchmarks (End of Each 4-Week Cycle)

Perform these tests in a fresh state (e.g. Day 28 or the following Monday):

Benchmark How to Test Record
Push-up max Max reps, strict form, stop when form breaks Total reps
KB Swing load Heaviest KB for 10 clean reps Weight used
DB RDL Heaviest 5 clean reps Weight per DB
Dead hang From pull-up bar or rings if available Time in seconds
Single-leg balance Stand on 1 leg, eyes closed Time per side

Monthly benchmarks tell you whether the programme is working. Strength gains should be visible over 2–3 cycles. Push-up reps may fluctuate with fatigue; swing and RDL loads should trend upward.

Nutrition Spot-Check (Once Per Week)

You do not need to log every meal every day. But once per week, log a full day to verify you are hitting targets. Use Cronometer or a similar app. Key things to check:
- Did protein hit 130g?
- Did total calories land ~2,100 on training days?
- Was fat above 40g (important for hormone production and D3/K2 absorption)?

7:20am  → 1 banana

7:32am  → Supersets begin

8:30am  → Leave for office

Shoulder Red Flags — Stop and Reassess

  • Sharp pain at any point during pressing movement
  • Pain that lingers more than 5 minutes post-set
  • Clicking/catching sensation under the acromion with overhead reach
  • Weakness on one side that was not present previously

If any of the above: skip remaining press sets that session, double the face pull volume, and if symptoms persist for >3 days, rest the shoulder completely for 5–7 days before returning to press movements.

Rucking Zone 2 Reference

Metric Target
Heart rate 107–125 bpm
Pace feel Can speak full sentences; breathing elevated but not gasping
Duration 35–45 min
Pack weight 8–10kg
Terrain Flat to moderate — avoid steep hills; inclines spike HR above Zone 2
Footwear Trail shoes or sturdy walking shoes — not running flats

Why you must not let HR spike above 125 bpm during rucking:

Zone 2 (107–125 bpm) is where the body trains the aerobic energy system most efficiently — it stimulates mitochondrial biogenesis (growth of new mitochondria in muscle cells) and develops the fat oxidation pathway. These are the long-term adaptations that improve cardiovascular health, metabolic efficiency, and longevity.

The moment HR crosses into Zone 3 (roughly 126–138 bpm), several things happen:
- Fuel source shifts — the body moves away from fat oxidation toward carbohydrate burning. You are no longer training the same system.
- Recovery cost rises sharply — Zone 3 is metabolically expensive. Unlike Zone 2, which you can recover from overnight, Zone 3 work accumulates fatigue over days. With 4 strength sessions already in the week, this erodes your capacity to train hard on Monday.
- No additional aerobic benefit — Zone 3 is sometimes called the "grey zone" because it is too easy to build VO2max (you need Zone 4–5 for that) and too hard to build aerobic base. It is the least productive intensity for your goals.

Practical control during Singapore rucking:
- If you hit a hill, slow your pace or take the hill at half-speed
- If HR spikes above 125, stop walking briefly (30–60 sec) until it drops back to 115, then resume
- In the morning heat (even at 7am), HR runs 5–10 bpm higher than in air-conditioning — factor this in and be willing to go slower than feels necessary

Time What
7:15am (training days only) Collagen 15g + Vit C
8:30am D3 4000 IU + K2 150mcg + Creatine 5g
7:00pm Omega-3 2g EPA+DHA + Zinc 30mg
9:15pm Magnesium glycinate 400mg
Post-workout (if needed) Whey 30g + 250ml milk

Monthly Plan — Female

4-Week Monthly Training & Nutrition Plan

40-Year-Old Singaporean Female — Fat Loss + Strength

1. Profile Summary

Attribute Detail
Age / Sex 40, female
Weight / Height 65 kg / 155 cm
BMI 27.1 (moderate excess body fat)
Training background 3 years yoga, Pilates, light strength — intermediate
Primary goal Fat loss
Secondary goal Significant strength gain
Training window 7:30 am – 12:30 pm (school pick-up at 12:30 pm)
Session length ~75 min
Equipment Mat, dumbbells, kettlebells, resistance bands
Injury notes Occasional knee and lower back pain — manageable, generally resolves

Why the programme is structured this way

Fat loss requires a sustained caloric deficit. However, without adequate protein and progressive resistance training, the body loses muscle alongside fat — a result that slows metabolism, reduces strength, and makes regaining fat more likely. This plan targets a modest deficit of 300–350 kcal/day, which supports roughly 0.5 kg of fat loss per week while preserving — and building — lean tissue.

The programming choices are deliberate:

  • McGill-safe core work (bird dog, McGill curl-up, side plank, dead bug) replaces traditional sit-ups and crunches, which load the lumbar spine in flexion. These alternatives are backed by Dr Stuart McGill's research and are far more effective at building spinal endurance without aggravating the lower back.
  • Knee loading is graduated: goblet squat is introduced before split squat; lateral band walks and clamshells are non-negotiable warm-up staples every lower body session to activate hip abductors and reduce knee valgus under load.
  • Hip flexor and glute work are treated as injury prevention, not optional extras. Tight hip flexors (especially psoas) contribute to anterior pelvic tilt and lower back pain. Strong glutes offload both the lumbar spine and the knee.
  • Turkish Get-Up (TGU) is included from Week 1. Your three years of yoga and Pilates are an asset here — TGU requires the exact kind of body awareness, breath control, and segmental stability that Pilates builds. You will pick this up faster than most beginners. Start light (4–6 kg) and treat it as a moving meditation rather than a strength exercise until the sequence is seamless.
  • Rucking on Thursday delivers Zone 2 cardiovascular training and bone density stimulus without the knee impact of running. Both benefits are particularly relevant for women approaching perimenopause, where oestrogen decline accelerates bone loss.
  • Sunday family swimming is counted as Zone 1–2 active recovery — no structure needed, just enjoy it.

2. Daily Supplement Schedule

Supplement Dose Timing Notes
Collagen (hydrolysed) 15 g 7:15 am — pre-workout Take with ~80 mg Vitamin C (1 kiwi or small glass of OJ). Shaw et al. research shows pre-exercise collagen + Vit C maximises tendon collagen synthesis by 3–4×. Critical for knee and connective tissue health.
Vitamin D3 3,000 IU With breakfast Take with fat for absorption — the eggs in your breakfast provide this. Singaporeans are frequently insufficient despite sun exposure due to indoor lifestyle and sunscreen use.
Vitamin K2 MK-7 150 mcg With breakfast alongside D3 K2 directs calcium to bones rather than arteries. Always pair with D3 at meaningful doses.
Whey protein isolate 25 g Post-workout (~8:30 am) Mix with 200 ml cold milk. Isolate preferred — minimal lactose, easier on digestion. Triggers muscle protein synthesis within the anabolic window.
Creatine monohydrate 3 g Post-workout with food (training days); with lunch (rest days) 3 g/day is effective for women — research supports the same absolute dose regardless of body weight for neuromuscular and cognitive benefits. No loading phase needed.
Omega-3 fish oil 2 g EPA+DHA With afternoon snack (~3:30 pm) Anti-inflammatory; supports joint health, fat loss, and mood. The fat in mixed nuts ensures absorption. Previously taken with dinner — now moved since dinner is a shake.
Zinc picolinate 20 mg With afternoon snack (~3:30 pm) Supports immune function, hormonal health, and recovery. Picolinate form is well-absorbed. Take with the nuts snack — never on an empty stomach.
Ashwagandha KSM-66 300 mg With afternoon snack (~3:30 pm) Clinically studied extract. Reduces cortisol, supports body composition, and improves sleep quality. Evening-adjacent timing still aligns with cortisol's natural afternoon decline.
Magnesium glycinate 320 mg 9:15 pm Glycinate form is gentle on digestion and highly bioavailable. Benefits: sleep quality, muscle relaxation, PMS symptom relief (cramping, mood), and cardiovascular health. Non-negotiable for active women.

Notes on what is intentionally excluded: No pre-workout stimulants (no caffeine). Collagen + Vit C provides a connective-tissue-focused pre-workout routine that is stimulant-free. Ashwagandha at dinner provides mild adaptogenic support without disrupting morning cortisol rhythms needed for energy.

5. The 4 Training Days (Detailed)

Day A — Lower Body + KB Swing

Monday, 7:30–8:45 am
Purpose: Posterior chain development (swings), knee-safe squat pattern, hip hinge, knee and hip prehabilitation, McGill-safe core training.
Movement patterns: Hinge, Squat, Core.

Warm-Up (10 min)

A longer warm-up is warranted given the knee and lower back history. Do not skip this.

  • Glute bridge — 2×15: Activates the glutes before loading. Lay on your back, feet flat, drive hips to ceiling, squeeze at the top for 1 sec.
  • Clamshell — 2×12/side: Hip abductor activation. Reduces knee valgus (inward collapse) under load. Use a light band around the knees if available.
  • Bodyweight goblet squat — 2×10: Practice the pattern before loading. Hold hands at chest. Push knees out, sit to comfortable depth.
  • Ankle dorsiflexion wall stretch — 30 sec/side: Limited ankle mobility causes knee forward travel to compensate — address this.
  • Cat-cow — 10 reps: Warm up lumbar and thoracic spine gently.

Main Work

  1. KB Swing
    - Key cues: "Hike" the KB back between your legs (like hiking a football), then drive through the heels and snap the hips forward explosively. The arms are just a pendulum — the power comes from the hips. Think "crush the ground" at the bottom. This is NOT a squat — the hips hinge back, not down.
    - The swing is the single best posterior chain conditioning exercise in this programme. It simultaneously trains hip hinge power, glute strength, and cardiovascular conditioning.

  2. KB Goblet Squat
    - Hold the KB at chest height with both hands cupping the bell. This front load forces an upright torso — far kinder to the lumbar spine than a back squat. Push the knees out over the toes. Depth to comfortable range; do not force range past the point where your lower back rounds.

  3. DB Romanian Deadlift (RDL)
    - Start LIGHT — 8–10 kg DBs in Week 1. The goal in early weeks is pattern, not load. Hinge at the hip (imagine a rod through your hips and the wall behind you), keep the back perfectly neutral, feel the hamstrings load. The bar traces the legs. Stop when you feel maximum hamstring stretch (usually just below the knee). Do not round the lower back.

  4. Clamshell + Lateral Band Walk
    - These are non-negotiable for knee health. The lateral band walk in particular directly strengthens the gluteus medius — the muscle that controls knee alignment. Use a light-to-medium band above the knees. 15 steps each direction.

Core Finisher (McGill-Safe)

  • McGill curl-up — 3×8: NOT a sit-up. Lie on your back. Place hands under the lumbar curve (you should feel a natural arch there — keep it). Curl only the head and shoulders slightly off the floor. Hold 8–10 sec. This trains anterior core without compressing the lumbar discs.
  • Bird dog — 3×8/side: On hands and knees. Extend one arm and the opposite leg simultaneously. Keep the spine absolutely still — no hip rotation, no sagging. Pause 3 sec at the top.
  • Side plank — 3×25–30 sec/side: From the forearm. Hips stacked. If this is too difficult, modify with the bottom knee on the floor.

Pilates Finisher (10 min)

  • Dead bug — 2×8/side: Lie on your back, arms to ceiling, hips and knees at 90°. Lower one arm and the opposite leg toward the floor simultaneously while maintaining back contact with the mat. Your Pilates background means you will understand the "imprint" position here.
  • Single-leg stretch — 2×10: Classic Pilates. Curl the head and shoulders up, draw one knee to chest, extend the other leg.
  • Spine stretch forward — 1×8: Seated, legs extended. Round forward from the crown of the head. Decompress the spine.

Day B — Upper Body + Turkish Get-Up

Tuesday, 7:30–8:50 am
Purpose: Pull and push patterns, TGU for full-body integration, shoulder health, Pilates core.
Movement patterns: Pull, Push, Full-body (TGU), Core.

Warm-Up (7 min)

  • Shoulder CARs (Controlled Articular Rotations) — 5 slow circles/arm: Move through the full rotator cuff range deliberately.
  • Band pull-apart — 2×20: Hold a light band at chest height, arms wide, pull it apart until it touches the chest. Activates rear deltoids and rotator cuff.
  • Cat-cow — 10 reps
  • Arm circles + wrist circles — 10 sec each direction

Main Work

  1. Turkish Get-Up (TGU)
    - Begin the session with TGU while your nervous system is fresh — technique breaks down when fatigued.
    - Start with 4–6 kg. Three reps per side, moving slowly.
    - The 6-phase sequence: (1) Roll to press — extend the arm, lock the elbow; (2) Roll to elbow — keep eyes on the bell; (3) Post to hand — press up through the shoulder; (4) Hip bridge — drive the hip high; (5) Sweep the leg through to the kneeling position; (6) Stand. Reverse for the descent.
    - Your yoga and Pilates background is a genuine advantage here. The body awareness required — the breath, the segmental control, the shoulder packing — are all skills you have been training for three years. TGU will feel more familiar than it does to most people who begin it. Be patient with the sequence and trust that fluency will come within two to three sessions.

  2. Single-arm DB Row
    - Place one knee and the same-side hand on a chair or box for support. Row the DB up toward the hip, not the shoulder. Feel the lat engage. Avoid rotating the torso. Heavy is fine here once the pattern is established.

  3. Push-up progression
    - Progress in this order: mat incline push-up (hands elevated) → standard push-up → archer push-up (one arm wider, loading shifts to that side).
    - Choose the variation where you can complete all reps with perfect form: body in a straight line from heel to crown, elbows at roughly 45° from the torso, chest touches the surface.

  4. DB Floor Press
    - Lie on the floor, DBs at chest height, elbows at 45°. Press to full extension. The floor limits shoulder ROM at the bottom — this makes it safer than a full bench press for people building shoulder strength, and the reduced ROM is protective for anyone with anterior shoulder sensitivity.

  5. Band Face Pull
    - Anchor a band to a door frame or sturdy furniture at face height. Pull toward the nose with elbows high and wide. Finish with external rotation (hands pull apart slightly at the end range). This is the most important shoulder health exercise in the programme. Do it every upper body session without exception.

Pilates Finisher (10 min)

  • The Hundred — 1×100 pumps: Lie on back, legs at 45° (or tabletop if needed), arms pumping by the sides. 5 pumps inhale, 5 pumps exhale. Maintain the curl of the head and shoulders.
  • Single-leg stretch — 2×10
  • Spine stretch + Swan — 2×8 each: Spine stretch rounds forward; Swan extends from prone — the combination works the spine in both directions.

Day C — Zone 2 Rucking + Conditioning Circuit

Thursday, 7:30–9:15 am
Purpose: Cardiovascular health, Zone 2 aerobic base, metabolic conditioning, active recovery for joints.
Movement patterns: Cardiovascular, Hinge, Push, Pull, Squat.

Rucking (35–40 min)

  • Load: Start at 5 kg; increase to 7 kg by Week 3.
  • Pace: Zone 2 — you should be able to speak in full sentences. Target heart rate: 108–126 bpm for age 40 (60–70% of HRmax). Use the talk test if you do not have a heart rate monitor.
  • Route: Neighbourhood loop or park. Start before 9 am to avoid Singapore heat and humidity.
  • Posture: Upright, shoulders back, pack sitting high on the back (not hanging low). Engage the core lightly throughout.
  • Why rucking specifically: Unlike running, rucking is low-impact on the knees while still providing a vertical compressive force on the skeleton — a key stimulus for maintaining bone density. For women approaching perimenopause, where oestrogen decline accelerates bone loss, this is a meaningful benefit. It also burns significantly more calories than walking (~2–3× more per hour) without the injury risk of running.

Post-Ruck Conditioning Circuit (20 min, 2 rounds)

Perform back-to-back with 90 sec rest between rounds. This is a metabolic finisher, not a strength session — keep weights moderate.

  • KB Swing: ×12
  • Push-up (or incline): ×10
  • Single-arm DB Row: ×10/side
  • Goblet Squat: ×10
  • Rest 90 sec

Mobility Finisher (10 min — addresses root causes of knee and lower back pain)

  • 90/90 hip mobility — 2 min: Sit in the 90/90 position (one hip internally rotated, one externally). Work through the end range gently.
  • World's greatest stretch — 3 reps/side: Lunge forward, place the same-side hand on the floor, rotate the opposite arm to the ceiling. Combines hip flexor stretch, thoracic rotation, and hamstring lengthening.
  • Couch stretch (kneeling hip flexor) — 60 sec/side: Rear foot on a sofa or chair, front leg at 90°. This targets the rectus femoris and psoas. Tight psoas pulls the lumbar spine into excessive extension (anterior pelvic tilt), which is one of the most common contributing factors to lower back pain. This stretch should be a daily habit.
  • Foam roller T-spine — 60 sec: Roller perpendicular to the spine at three levels (lower thoracic, mid thoracic, upper thoracic). Arms crossed over chest. Gently extend over the roller. Do not roll the lower back.

Day D — Full Body Strength + Carry

Friday, 7:30–8:50 am
Purpose: Full-body integration, loaded carry, single-leg strength, anti-rotation core.
Movement patterns: Power/Full-body, Single-Leg, Pull, Carry, Core.

Warm-Up (7 min)

  • Hip hinge drill (bodyweight) — 2×10: Stand with feet hip-width. Push hips back as far as possible while keeping the back flat. Touch fingers to mid-shin. Stand and repeat. Feel the hamstrings load.
  • Thoracic rotation in quadruped — 10/side: On hands and knees, one hand behind the head, rotate the elbow to the ceiling. Warms up the thoracic spine for the pressing movement.
  • Glute bridge — 2×15
  • Band pull-apart — 2×15

Main Work

  1. KB Single-arm Clean + Press
    - Start with 8 kg. The clean: hinge and "hike" the KB, then aggressively pull the elbow high as the hips extend, "catching" the KB in the rack position (bell resting on the forearm, elbow tucked to ribs). From rack: press straight overhead to full lockout. Lower back to rack, then hinge and park the KB.
    - This is a full-body power chain exercise — hips generate the energy, the shoulder completes it. It is excellent for fat loss because it demands coordination, power, and stability simultaneously.

  2. Bulgarian Split Squat
    - Rear foot elevated on a chair behind you, DBs held at sides. Lower the back knee toward the floor under control. Depth to comfortable range — do not push through knee discomfort. The front foot does the work. This is the most challenging single-leg exercise in the programme, so start with light DBs (or bodyweight) and earn the load gradually.

  3. DB Bent-over Row
    - Both arms simultaneously. Hinge at the hip (maintain the back angle throughout the set), pull the DBs to the lower rib cage. This can be loaded heavier than the single-arm row because you have bilateral stability.

  4. KB or DB Farmer Carry
    - 3×20 m. Measure out a corridor or garden path. Hold a KB or DB in each hand, stand tall, brace the core, and walk. This exercise is deceptively hard and carries outsized benefits: grip strength, core bracing under load, posture, and trap development.

  5. Band Pallof Press
    - Anchor a band to a door frame or sturdy furniture at chest height. Stand sideways to the anchor. Hold the band at chest with both hands. Press directly forward to full arm extension, hold 2 sec, return. The band tries to rotate you — resist it. This is anti-rotation core training, which is more functional than most traditional ab exercises.

Cool-Down (10 min)

  • Foam roller: IT band (side of thigh), quads, glutes — key for knee maintenance.
  • 90/90 hip — 1 min/side
  • Child's pose + thoracic extension — hold each 30–60 sec

6. The 4-Week Undulating Periodisation

Week Phase Sets Reps RPE Notes
Week 1 Technique + Accumulation 3 10 6–7 Master movement patterns. Lighter loads. Feel comfortable with TGU and swings. The goal this week is not fatigue — it is fluency.
Week 2 Build 4 8 7–8 Increase loads. Technique should be solid. Add one set across most exercises. You should feel challenged but not crushed.
Week 3 Volume 4 10–12 7–8 More total reps. Metabolic stress. Slightly lighter than Week 2 per set, but more total volume. Expect to feel this in the 48 hours after sessions.
Week 4 Deload 2 10 5 50% volume. Same exercises. Light and technical. This is not a "lazy week" — it is when adaptation consolidates. Use extra time for mobility work.

KB Swing Weekly Progression

Week Sets × Reps Notes
Week 1 3×12 Technique focus — nail the hip hinge and explosive extension
Week 2 4×12 Add a set; increase KB weight if Week 1 felt easy
Week 3 4×15 More reps per set; same or slightly lighter KB
Week 4 2×10 Deload; lighter KB or fewer reps; stay grooved

Rucking Weekly Progression

Week Pack Weight Duration Notes
Week 1 5 kg 35 min Establish the habit and pace
Week 2 5 kg 40 min Add 5 minutes
Week 3 7 kg 35 min Increase load, reduce duration
Week 4 5 kg 30 min Deload — lighter, shorter

8. Progressive Overload Guidelines

When to add weight:
Complete all prescribed sets and reps at RPE ≤6 for two consecutive sessions → increase weight. For dumbbells: add 1–2 kg. For kettlebells: move to the next bell size. Do not chase weight — chase technique.

Knee rule:
If goblet squat causes knee pain during or after the session, reduce depth to the point that is pain-free. If pain persists at any depth, substitute a box squat: sit back onto a chair and stand. This removes the need to control the descent and is a safe bridge exercise while the knee is sensitive.

Lower back rule:
If the RDL causes lower back pain, reduce weight significantly and revisit the hip hinge pattern. Film yourself from the side if possible. If pain persists despite lightening the load, substitute the hip thrust: sit your back against a sofa, feet flat, drive the hips up to full extension. The hip thrust is glute-dominant and places minimal load on the lumbar spine.

TGU rule:
Do not increase KB weight until you can complete all 6 phases on both sides with smooth, unhurried movement. Rushing the TGU with a weight you cannot control defeats its purpose. The movement should feel like a deliberate sequence, not a struggle.

Deload rule:
Take a deload week every fourth week regardless of how you feel. The adaptations from hard training occur during recovery, not during the sessions themselves.

9. Fat Loss Tracking

Weekly Weigh-In Protocol

  • Weigh every Sunday morning, post-void, before eating or drinking
  • Wear minimal or no clothing for consistency
  • Log the number — do not react emotionally to a single reading; look for the trend over 3–4 weeks

Expected Rate of Loss

  • Target: 0.3–0.5 kg/week — this is the sustainable, muscle-preserving range
  • 0.3 kg/week = ~100 g fat lost per day at the cellular level — genuinely meaningful over a month
  • Over this 4-week programme: expect 1.2–2.0 kg of fat loss if the plan is followed consistently

Adjustments

Scenario Action
Losing >0.7 kg/week Add 100 kcal/day — risk of muscle loss at faster rate. Add to breakfast (extra egg or slightly more milk).
No loss after 2 full weeks Reduce lunch carbs by half: ¼ cup brown rice instead of ½ cup. This is the first and simplest lever to pull.
Scale not moving but measurements decreasing Continue as-is — this is body recomposition (fat loss + muscle gain). Common in the first 4–6 weeks of a new programme.
Very hungry on rest days Add a small protein snack (100 g cottage cheese or 1 hard-boiled egg) — this is preferable to eating off-plan.

Monthly Measurements

Take on Day 1 and Day 28, same time of day (morning, before eating):
- Waist: at the narrowest point, just above the navel
- Hip: at the widest point across the buttocks
- Thigh: at the mid-thigh of the dominant leg, measured from the same anatomical landmark each time

Scale weight alone misses the most important changes happening in your body. A month of consistent training and appropriate nutrition will almost certainly produce visible changes in measurements and how clothes fit, even if the scale moves less than expected (especially in the early weeks as muscles adapt and glycogen stores shift).

Notes for Long-Term Progress

This 4-week plan is designed to be repeatable with progressive loading. After Week 4 (deload), begin again from Week 1 of the same structure — but with heavier loads than you started this cycle. Every 4 weeks you will be measurably stronger than the previous cycle.

Three months of consistent application of this plan — with honest nutrition adherence and progressive loading — will produce a transformation in both body composition and physical capacity that three more years of yoga and Pilates alone would not. The combination of resistance training, adequate protein, modest caloric deficit, and Zone 2 cardio is one of the most evidence-based approaches to body composition improvement in the scientific literature for women.

The knee and lower back issues you experience are not a barrier — they are a signal. This programme addresses their root causes (weak glutes, tight hip flexors, poor anterior core endurance) directly. Most people with similar presentations find that pain frequency and severity decrease significantly within 6–8 weeks of consistent hip/glute work and McGill core training.

Finally: the Sunday family swim is not optional. It is one of the best things in this programme.
